Local News

### Cornerstone Laying Ceremony Held Yesterday for New Municipal Government Building 240

Mayor Zhang Qun and Huang Fu deliver important speeches

Various circles, both Chinese and foreign, participate in grand ceremony

New building to be completed by the end of next year

The Shanghai Municipal Government, near the newly developed city center area, is constructing a new municipal government building. The estimated cost is 500,000 yuan. Yesterday morning at 10 o'clock, Mayor Zhang laid the cornerstone, with the expectation of completion by the end of next year. Over a thousand people from various circles, both Chinese and foreign, participated in the grand ceremony. Zhang Qun, Huang Fu, Shen Yi, Yu Qiaqing, Wang Xiaolai, and Ye Gongchuo delivered successive speeches, all recognizing the laying of the cornerstone of the new municipal government building as the beginning of the construction of the city center area, and also the starting point for the implementation of Sun Yat-sen's Greater Shanghai Plan. The ceremony concluded at noon.

[Photograph of Cornerstone Laying Ceremony for New Municipal Government Building taken by this newspaper]

Participating Guests 241

Yesterday, the drizzling rain had just cleared, and the weather was still muggy. Secretary-General Yu, the various bureau chiefs, and all the staff were on hand to receive guests. Those from various circles, both Chinese and foreign, who continuously arrived to participate in the grand ceremony included: Central Supervisory Committee Member Cai Yuanpei, first Shanghai Mayor Huang Fu, former Minister of Transportation Ye Gongchuo, Jiangsu Pacification Commissioner Zhang Zhijiang, Envoy to Germany Jiang Zuobin, Envoy to France Qian Xinzhi, Jiangsu Higher Court Second Branch President Xu Weizhen, Shanghai Special District Local Court Representative Ju Zhijing, Fudan University President Li Denghui, Tongji University President Hu Shuhua, Ministry of Foreign Affairs Shanghai Office Director Yang Nianzu, Songhu Garrison Headquarters Chief of Staff Xu Jinyuan, Shanghai County Magistrate Yan Shenyu, Shanghai Chamber of Commerce President Wang Xiaolai, Banking Association Representative Lin Kanghou, Zhabei Defense Corps Commander Wang Binyan, Public Works Bureau Chinese Director Yuan Ludeng, Yu Qiaqing, China Merchants Steam Navigation Company General Manager Guo Wai-feng, Bank of China President Zhang Gongquan, Shanghai Bank President Chen

### Photo of the New Municipal Government Building's Cornerstone (Taken by This Newspaper) 242

Guangfu, Shen Bao General Manager Shi Liangcai, Shen Bao Manager Zhang Zhuping, Japanese Acting Consul-General Shigemitsu, Cuban Envoy Pe de Lai, Czech Envoy Fei Fan'er, British Consul-General Bailey Naman, Japanese Consul-General Murai, German Consul-General Klembach, Dutch Consul-General Kraumann, Public Works Bureau Director-General Fessenden, Shanghai International Settlement Volunteer Corps Commander Thomson, and over a thousand others.

Grand Occasion During the Ceremony 243

The venue was located between Sanmin Road and Wuquan Road. At the east and west entrances, tall archways resembling city walls were erected. On the right side of the road, two reed mat sheds were built. One was a drawing room, with many drawings of municipal buildings and residences hanging inside. The other was a model room, storing models of the Municipal Government and the Finance Bureau, as well as a complete model of the Greater Shanghai Plan. A large platform was erected to the south of the venue. The venue was covered with national flags and equipped with amplified microphones. In the center of the cornerstone laying platform was a cornerstone, about four English feet in cube. At 10:15 AM, the Municipal Public Security Bureau Military Band played music, opening the meeting. Mayor Zhang presided over the meeting, following the established protocols. The chairman delivered an opening speech. Public Works Bureau Director Shen Yi reported on the preparations. Guests Huang Yingbai, Yu Qiaqing, Ye Gongchuo, and Wang Xiaolai delivered successive speeches. Then music was played, guiding the audience to the cornerstone laying platform on the opposite side, where Mayor Zhang performed the cornerstone laying ceremony. Afterwards, a rectangular copper box, about one and a half English feet long and one English foot wide, containing various souvenirs, was buried in the center of the cornerstone with cement. Then the ceremony was declared complete and the meeting adjourned. The inscription on the cornerstone read: "July 7th, 20th Year of the Republic of China, Shanghai Municipal Government Cornerstone Laying Commemoration, Shanghai Mayor Zhang Qun." The souvenirs stored in the copper box in the cornerstone were: New Municipal Government Building Contract and Explanations, City Center Area Plan Outline Solicitation for Municipal Government Designs, Complete Set of Municipal Government Drawings, City Center Area Opinion Papers, City Center Area Land Reclamation Measures, City Center Area Plan Outline, City Center Area Construction Committee Work Report, Public Works Report, Shen Bao Pictorial Weekly, and the News Paper Cornerstone Laying Special Issue.

Mayor Zhang's Speech 244

After the ceremony, Chairman and Mayor Zhang delivered an opening speech, saying: "Distinguished guests, today the Shanghai Municipal Government is holding the cornerstone laying ceremony for the new building in the city center area. I am extremely grateful for your presence in the summer heat to offer guidance. Shanghai is one of the world's renowned commercial ports, and its importance goes without saying. Since the National Government established its capital in Nanjing, it has been recognized that special efforts in municipal administration are necessary to meet the needs of the times and achieve the goal of building a Greater Shanghai. Therefore, on July 7th of the 16th year of the Republic of China, the establishment of Shanghai Special Municipality and the Municipal Government was initiated, and it has been four years now. Recalling the beginning of the founding, the first Mayor, Mr. Huang Yingbai, was the popular choice of the time. His grand plans and regulations were also a model for later generations, worthy of lasting influence. In April of the 18th year, I was entrusted with the responsibility of this municipality. I deeply felt the importance of my duties and dared not be negligent or idle. Because I recognized the rapid increase in the city's population and the skyrocketing land prices, the housing problem for the citizens was the most difficult to solve. As for transportation, the land and water facilities had no connection, causing much inconvenience for travelers and cargo transportation. Moreover, the concessions running through the entire city hindered the central government's administrative facilities and development in this city. After careful research and planning by my colleagues, it was proposed in July of the 17th year of the Republic of China to designate more than 5,000 acres of land north of Xiangyin Road, south of Zhayin Road, east of Songhu Road, and west of the Ten Yitu of Zhounan as the construction area of the City Center. After being submitted to the Municipal Government Meeting Construction Discussion Committee for approval, it was reported to the Central Government for approval. This area is adjacent to Wusong in the north, connected to the concessions in the south, leads to the Huangpu River in the east, and is close to the railway in the west. The transportation is very convenient. It is the most suitable location in the entire city. Once the ideal commercial port is built and the railway lines are reorganized, the prosperity of future undertakings can be expected in the near future. After completing the necessary procedures, the Municipal Government established the City Center Area Construction Committee, recruited professional talents, and tasked them with handling the matter, still under the leadership of the Director of the Public Works Bureau. Over the past year, concrete plans have been formulated, such as the allocation of administrative, commercial, dock, and residential areas, which have been planned separately. In addition, the important trunk roads connecting the docks, railways, and various urban areas have also been specified in detail, approved, and implemented. Several roads have already started construction or will soon start construction. From now on, progressing in order, this desolate and barren area will become prosperous and completely transformed in a few years. As for the organization within the area, models from various countries' municipal administrations have been adopted and adapted to our country's society. Facilities such as parks, stadiums, and other equipment related to human health are required to be complete. Furthermore, a portion of the land in the area, about 800 acres, which is the most valuable and easily developed, will be publicly reclaimed at the original land acquisition price, including the necessary expenses for road construction and drainage. The purpose is nothing more than to allow citizens to enjoy the benefits of the city center area, and the Municipal Government will not charge excessive fees. As for construction, the most suitable house building styles will be solicited for builders to choose and refer to. At the same time, citizens will be encouraged to operate and build, in order to promote the development of the City Center. Furthermore, the design of the new commercial port is also in active planning. The location is near Wusong Town, where the river is deepest, which facilitates the berthing of giant ships and also facilitates connection with the railway. Regarding the railway issue, discussions are also underway with the Ministry of Railways to implement more convenient methods in the future. In addition, a new dock area is planned at a deep-water location in the east of the City Center area to meet current needs. The above plans will surely be realized in a considerable amount of time. As for the content of each plan, due to time constraints, a detailed report cannot be given today. If you would like to know the details, please refer to various publications and today's report by the Director of the Public Works Bureau. Finally, I have one more thing to say to all the guests: this City Center area is the city center area of the entire Shanghai city, not the city center area of the Municipal Government. Therefore, regarding construction issues, I hope that all citizens and the Municipal Government will jointly bear this important responsibility. The Municipal Government will act as the vanguard, first building office buildings here. Starting from the day of today's cornerstone laying ceremony, construction will be completed within one and a half years. Various subsidiary structures and necessary equipment will also be carried out simultaneously. In January of the following year, the Municipal Government colleagues will be able to move here to work, so as to supervise and promote the success of the construction of this area. However, at the beginning of construction, many things need to be carried out. The talents and resources of my colleagues are limited, and I am deeply afraid that we will not be able to achieve perfection. I hope that all of you will provide guidance and correct our shortcomings. Today is the fourth anniversary of the establishment of the Municipal Government. We will never forget the pioneering spirit of the first Mayor, Mr. Huang Yingbai. I have specially invited Mr. Huang to come here from Moganshan to participate in the ceremony and provide guidance. I would like to introduce him to everyone so that you can listen to Mr. Huang's remarks."

Director Shen's Speech 245

Director of the Bureau of Public Works, Shen Yi, gave a speech about the Shanghai Municipal Government's preparations for building new houses, saying: Although the construction of new municipal government buildings and the development of the city center area have been advocated by the Shanghai Municipal Government for just over a year, the motivation can be traced back to four years ago. When the Municipal Government was established in July of the 16th year of the Republic of China, the first mayor of this city, Mr. Huang Yingbai, realized that the previous municipal administration was corrupt and that thorough reform plans were necessary for rectification. Therefore, on the one hand, he sought to fully consolidate the organization of the ten bureaus of the Municipal Government, and on the other hand, he first requested the Central Government to determine the scope of the city area, including Wusong, Jiangwan, Dachang, Yanghang, and other districts. The above two points have a close relationship with the subsequent development of municipal administration in this city. Mayor Huang resigned less than two months after taking office, and Mr. Zhang Boxuan succeeded him as mayor. All undertakings continued as before. In November of the 16th year of the Republic of China, a Design Committee was established to study various municipal issues. In order to understand the current situation of each city area, in July of the 17th year of the Republic of China, he led the directors of each bureau to inspect each city area and conduct on-site surveys. At the same time, a part of the city area was taken over, making the selection of the city center area directly under the Municipal Government largely related to this. It was unexpected that the new municipal government buildings could be based here today, which is deeply memorable. At that time, it was realized that the Municipal Government was remotely located in western Shanghai, and the bureaus were scattered throughout the city. The transmission of documents was time-consuming, and citizens found it particularly inconvenient to travel back and forth. Therefore, there was a plan to build municipal government buildings. In September of the 17th year of the Republic of China, a Preparatory Committee for the Construction of Municipal Government Buildings was established. Later, because the construction of the Municipal Government required a large amount of money, which was not easy to realize at that time, and the School of Arts and Crafts opposite the Xinpu Yutang in southern Shanghai had been closed for a long time, it was quite suitable for the offices of the Municipal Government and its bureaus. Therefore, in November of the 17th year of the Republic of China, it was decided to formally lease the school, and a contract was signed at the end of that year, with March 1 of the 18th year of the Republic of China as the date of relocation. Soon after, Mayor Zhang Boxuan resigned, and the matter was suspended. When Mayor Zhang Yuejun took office, he made the construction of a new city area his ambition. He believed that borrowing the School of Arts and Crafts as office buildings for the Municipal Government and its bureaus was not a thorough solution, as it was uneconomical and would indefinitely prolong the construction of new municipal government buildings. Therefore, he advocated not moving temporarily, but actively planning the new city area and preparing to build new municipal government buildings. This was in April of the 18th year of the Republic of China. In July of the 18th year of the Republic of China, the plan for the city center area was announced, and the City Center Area Construction Committee was established. At the same time, the Municipal Government Construction Committee was abolished, and all matters related to the construction of the Municipal Government were transferred to the City Center Area Construction Committee for handling. Mayor Yuejun also believed that the city center area was still a vacant lot, and he was deeply concerned that investors would hesitate to move forward, which would affect the future development. Therefore, he resolutely advocated building municipal government buildings in the city center area first to promote it, and designated funds from the first municipal public bond issued in this city to be used for operating the city center area. On the one hand, the City Center Area Construction Committee selected the location for the new buildings, engaged in planning, and in order to gather ideas and broaden benefits, in January of the 19th year of the Republic of China, a reward was offered for the design of the municipal government buildings. In July of the 19th year of the Republic of China, an architect's office was established to draw up formal plans, and architect Dong Dayou was hired to take charge. In May of the 20th year of the Republic of China, bidding began, and the Zhu Senji Construction Company won the bid for 548,000 yuan. Construction officially began in early June and is expected to be completed by the end of the 21st year of the Republic of China. The new building is more than 30 meters high, more than 90 meters long, and 25 meters wide. The exterior adopts the Chinese architectural style. The building has four floors. The ground floor is for offices, a cafeteria, etc. The second floor is for the auditorium, conference room, and library. The third floor is all offices. The fourth floor is for archives and storage rooms. After the construction is completed, in addition to the secretariat, it can accommodate approximately two bureaus for office work. The remaining bureaus will temporarily build temporary houses to the north of the new municipal government buildings, which will also begin construction soon. On the occasion of the groundbreaking ceremony, I respectfully report the preparations as follows.

Huang Yingbai's Speech 246

The Shanghai Municipal Government has been established for four years, and today is exactly the beginning of the fifth year. It is also the date for the groundbreaking ceremony of the new municipal government buildings. Mayor Yuejun insisted on inviting me to attend because I have a two-time historical relationship with Shanghai in the first year of the Republic of China and the sixteenth year of the Republic of China. Therefore, I came down from the mountain a few days ago to participate in this grand event, and I feel a limited amount of pleasure in my heart. Now, I will briefly share with you my thoughts. Shanghai is a major port for trade between China and foreign countries, with many railways and merchants gathering here. It has become one of the world's largest commercial ports. In recent years, its development has been particularly rapid, and I heard that the population has reached three million, ranking first among all cities in the country. Politically speaking, since the National Government established its capital in Nanjing, it has implicitly grasped the center of national politics, economy, and diplomacy. Geographically speaking, Shanghai is the gateway to the Yangtze River and the shield of the southeast, possessing the qualifications of both a military port and a commercial port. The National Government, recognizing its important position, explicitly promulgated Shanghai as a special city in the summer of the sixteenth year of the Republic of China. Although the name of special city no longer exists, its special nature does not change due to the name. However, Shanghai has a concession with more than eighty years of history. What is now called Shanghai is actually more than half of its essence within the concession area. What is a concession? Why does it exist only in our country? What are the advantages and disadvantages of the concession for our country? In recent years, the inland has become increasingly impoverished. Why can the concession accelerate its prosperity? These questions cannot be answered in a short speech. What can be said is that the existence of concessions in our country originated from a treaty of "necessity". For the past eighty years, those who praise it call it a medium for Western civilization, and those who slander it call it tuberculosis of the Republic of China. In fact, everything is intricate and cannot be observed simply. Civilization is a medium, and so is evil. Microbes cause disease, and microbes can also cure disease. This is why the contradictory phenomenon of the Shanghai concession is formed: everyone slanders it, but it flourishes every year. However, microbial treatment is ultimately a temporary and necessary measure, while the medium of evil is a great danger to the country. Today, people strongly advocate the recovery of concessions. They do not know that forcible seizure is not only impossible, but also feels inappropriate. Begging not only will not be allowed by others, but also puts us in what position? Li Wenzhong once said that there is no diplomacy in the international arena, only self-reliance. For example, in dealing with friends, each other must have considerable qualifications. I want to contact him, and he also wants to contact me, and then we can be called friends. If I have no foothold and only want to rely on others, even if I speak eloquently, it will be useless. When I first arrived in Shanghai, foreign soldiers were very rare and arrogant, thinking that I must rely on them completely. They hesitated and watched, intending to coerce me. They saw that our soldiers looked tattered and laughed, saying that they were a group of beggars and how could they fight. I ignored them and used my own army to fight. After fighting a few times, they saw that we had some ability and gradually wanted to come forward. I asked them even less. Later, we won even more battles, and our military reputation was greatly enhanced. Seeing that I did not ask for their help, they felt that it was meaningless and came again and again to ask to volunteer. I said that it would be good to help me fight, but they must be under my command and control, and the rewards and punishments for merits and demerits must be according to military orders. They agreed one by one and then I used them. They really obeyed the agreement and made great contributions. Gordon also gained a great reputation. If my own army was not good enough, they might not help even if I asked. If they did help, it would become a case of the guest taking over the host, and I don't know how much convenience they would take and how many hidden dangers they would leave behind. Alas, our country's future handling of the Shanghai concession issue is the same. We can know what to do. As mentioned above, the important position of Shanghai is so important, and its relationship is so complex. Therefore, the construction of Shanghai is a common and urgent need for the country and the local area. When implementing the construction, we must also consider national defense, industry, commerce, transportation, and territorial integrity. The significance is far-reaching, and the responsibility is heavy. It is completely different from ordinary municipal facilities. The most suitable location for the Shanghai city center area, based on the situation of Wusong Port, should be the area east of Jiangwan Town, which is the location currently selected by the Municipal Government. It can centrally control the north of Wusong Port and the south of the Shanghai urban area. When the Jiangqiao Bridge is completed in the future, it will be even more convenient for the development and facilities of Pudong. The reason why the concession did not select this location in the past may be because it was too far from the city, there was a lack of workers, transportation was inconvenient, and trade was scarce. They had to accommodate the facts and start with the area near the city, along the Huangpu River, which is now called the Bund. If this location had been selected in the past, I know that in these eighty years, half of it would have been due to the needs of reality and half of it would have been due to the perfection of planning. Gradually, the concession would have been connected to Wusong, like Go, forming a corner on its own. We would have no room to add a living eye. Therefore, this city center area can be said to be a suitable land specially left by heaven, giving us the opportunity to renew ourselves and extricate ourselves. This is what people across the country should cherish, support, and promote. The construction of Shanghai is a common and urgent need for the country and the local area. I have said this before. But do we hope that the national financial resources will be used for construction? I am afraid that with so many construction projects urgently needed across the country, we cannot focus all our efforts on one corner. Or do we hope that local financial resources will be used for construction? Facts show that the mere three million Shanghai citizens cannot shoulder the heavy responsibility of the whole country. Therefore, I believe that we should divide national affairs and local affairs into two categories. Local affairs should naturally be borne by local financial resources, such as public security, sanitation, primary and secondary education, land consolidation, public utilities, civil engineering, and all industrial, commercial, and other social affairs. As for national affairs, except for the fortification equipment, which should be directly responsible by the military department, and the location of the station, which should be jointly determined with the railway department, and the railway department should implement it on a regular basis, the remaining items, such as wharf construction, water and land transportation, and Jiangqiao construction, are local affairs with the nature of national affairs. The government should subsidize the shortage of local financial resources with national financial resources, designate funds, and allocate them to the Municipal Government on a regular basis, so that it will be easy to do things and it will be reasonable. In short, Shanghai is not only Shanghai for Shanghai people, but also Shanghai for the whole country, which has a major impact on politics, economy, industry, trade, diplomacy, and military affairs. If all construction projects are considered to be what Shanghai citizens should have, and the Shanghai Municipal Government does not consider itself to be the government of Shanghai, but considers itself to be the municipal government, then it would be a big mistake. At the same time, colleagues in the Municipal Government should pay attention to the cultural construction, moral construction, discipline construction, and order construction of the new Shanghai during the process of material construction. Otherwise, ten or twenty years later, even if the material construction is brilliantly prepared and completely matches the current concession, ask whether the spiritual life and material life of the citizens living in the concession today are consistently satisfactory? I know that it will not be the case. We often travel to major cities in Europe and the United States, and most of them have what is called the upper city and the lower city. The lower city has chimneys like forests, wharves like combs, clerks, workers, and heavily loaded trucks coming and going on the road, like weaving. The upper city has beautiful residences, great universities, solemn churches, quiet parks, magnificent libraries, and noble entertainment venues gathered together to form another world. In the city, whether it is the upper or lower city, not only are there no armed soldiers, but there are also few police officers with guns. However, the residents and travelers all have a sense of living and working in peace and contentment, and being active and enterprising. Alas, enriching and educating people at the same time, and spiritual life and material life are advancing together, is why Europe and the United States have become Europe and the United States. Fortunately, Shanghai

Page 14

Although the Municipal Government has often suffered from the lack of unified administration since its establishment, it has been able to refer to both theory and practice, and respond and deal with it appropriately, either by welcoming or rejecting. Although the military has not yet ended its financial exhaustion, it has still been able to improve the old urban area and promote the new urban area within its reach. Its achievements are seen by us, and the ideal of the Shanghai city center area plan for several years is now beginning to be implemented. This is a gratifying phenomenon. I believe that today it is more appropriate to consider the founding of the new city hall, and to consider it the founding of the city center area. If we can achieve the expectations mentioned above, and get the central government's subsidies, the nation's love, the citizens' trust, and the continued efforts of the colleagues in the Municipal Government, I know that the speed of the results and the impact will be greater than what can be imagined today. Recalling what I said four years ago today, when I took office as the first mayor of this city, I said, "In addition to the goal of building a great Shanghai, we must not allow those who want to occupy our territorial sovereignty for a long time to use it as an excuse. We must not allow those who are jealous of our party's success to say that all slogans and all doctrines are an unredeemed paper currency." Although I made this statement, I soon left, so that the "Greater Shanghai" banknote I issued could not be redeemed. Fortunately, the successors, such as former Mayor Zhang Boxuan, today's Mayor Yuejun, and all colleagues in the Municipal Government, have been able to maintain the credit of the banknote, and Mayor Yuejun is even preparing to start redeeming it. Therefore, I am here today to participate in the ceremony, and the kind of joy in my heart is indescribable. The ancients said, "Its beginning is simple, and its end will be huge." I dare to borrow this saying to wish the success of the city center area of Greater Shanghai. Xuan Yuqiaqing, Wang Xiaoyu, and Ye Gongchuo gave speeches on behalf of the citizens, which are omitted.

Righteous and Stern

City Chamber of Commerce Telegram 248

The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce sent a telegram to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs in Nanjing, saying: The Japanese are using the Wanbaoshan incident to instigate Koreans to persecute overseas Chinese, in order to alienate the feelings between China and Korea and achieve their goal of invading the East Province. The basis for Korean migration to China is Article 3 of the Sino-Korean Border Affairs Treaty of the Tujingmen in the first year of Xuantong. According to this article, the so-called Chinese government still allows Koreans to reside in the cultivated land north of the Tumen River, which only refers to the places already cultivated north of the Tumen River in the first year of Xuantong, and allows them to continue to reside there. It is not a limitless permit for them to continue to occupy and cultivate land in the future. Therefore, the fact that Korean farmers have arbitrarily occupied and cultivated paddy fields in the two provinces of Liaoning and Jilin is actually because the authorities of the province failed to adhere to the Tumen River Treaty and only sought to gain a false reputation for appeasement. Looking back at the Japanese in Korea, on the one hand, they secretly induce Koreans to promote anti-Chinese sentiment, and on the other hand, they restrict Chinese workers with orders from the Governor-General's Office, doing everything possible. Therefore, the plan to get to the root of the matter today is to imitate the Sino-French Special Treaty on Vietnamese Commerce and formulate a special treaty on reciprocal trade between overseas Chinese and Koreans in Korea. There should be restrictions on the number and area of ​​cultivating farmers and immigrants, and the principle of mutual immigration should be determined. Before this special treaty is signed, the Tumen River Border Treaty should be strictly observed, and new immigrants should not be allowed to cultivate beyond the border, so as to avoid disputes at any time and place. As for the situation of hostility towards Chinese in Incheon and other places, your ministry should telegraph the Japanese ambassador and resident consuls in Korea to properly negotiate and protect them. Incheon is close to the coast, and warships can reach it. If it can be negotiated by the Bohai Fleet to send ships to patrol, it will also be enough to comfort the overseas Chinese. This Month, Second Day: Outer Mongolian Troops Shoot at Eurasia Aviation Company's Northbound Aircraft Number Two During Descent 253

Aircraft Now Found Safe and Sound

Pilot and Mechanic Seem to Be Captured

According to Li Jingcong, Director of Operations at Eurasia Aviation Company, the company received urgent telegrams from Manzhouli on the third and fourth of this month, reporting that the Eurasia Number Two aircraft, scheduled to fly on Thursday, the second of this month, had not arrived. Simultaneously, a report from Linxi stated that the aircraft had departed on time, leading to the conclusion that the aircraft must have encountered an obstacle between Linxi and Manzhouli. On the fifth and sixth, two aircraft, Eurasia One and Eurasia Three, were dispatched to search the area. According to the report from the pilot of Eurasia One, Eurasia Number Two was found in Outer Mongolian territory. The aircraft is safe and sound, but the pilot and mechanic seem to have been captured. The aircraft attempted to land and provide assistance, but was met with heavy fire from Mongolian soldiers, making it impossible. The company was astonished upon hearing this news. When I (Li referring to himself) and Shi Mide, the Director of the Air Navigation Section, first conducted the straight-line trial flight from Duolun to Manzhouli, it was clear that this route would inevitably pass through Outer Mongolian territory. Fearing that this would easily lead to various misunderstandings, we subsequently took a second flight, detouring through Linxi towards Manzhouli. According to the maps drawn by China and other countries, this route does not require passing through Outer Mongolian territory. Therefore, we decided to change the route to fly from Linxi to Manzhouli. From the trial flight to the official opening of the route, for at least two or three months, there were no obstacles, proving that we did not pass through Outer Mongolian territory. Now, it has been forced to descend because it flew over Outer Mongolian territory. The reasons for this are likely to be one of the following two: (1) When the Number Two aircraft flew out of Linxi, it had to detour through Outer Mongolian territory due to weather conditions; (2) It was forced to descend due to heavy fire from Mongolian soldiers after passing through Outer Mongolian territory. Fortunately, the company is commercial in nature, and the aircraft used are all for postal transport. The routes and markings used are already known to all countries in the world, and Outer Mongolia must also have heard of them. After inspection, it should be released. Currently, the company is still actively trying to rescue the crew. The mail bound for Europe carried that day will not be delivered on time. The company has formally reported this to the post office today.

Sino-Cuban Joint Sugar Factory 254

Ministry of Industry in Talks with Cuban Sugar Merchants

Preliminary Agreement Now Signed, Progressing Actively

Regarding the Sino-Cuban joint venture for establishing a large-scale sugar factory in Shanghai, which the Ministry of Industry is currently pursuing, Minister of Industry Kong Xiangxi told reporters yesterday that this matter is being negotiated and carried out by the Ministry of Industry and Cuban sugar merchants, not with the Cuban government. The capital is set at US$5 million, and the main factory will be located in Shanghai. Both parties have already signed a preliminary agreement. The Cuban sugar merchants have now left Shanghai to return to their country. Once the National Government has reviewed and approved the preliminary agreement, they will come to Shanghai to sign a formal contract. The Ministry of Industry conducted a detailed investigation before handling this matter. According to customs import statistics, the first item is of course yarn, and the second is sugar. Even for China with its 400 million people, according to precise statistics, the average person uses 0.3 to 0.45 yuan of sugar per month, so the quantity needed is enormous. Therefore, establishing a sugar factory is an urgent matter to solve the problem. Kong departed for Beijing last night by night train.

Fifth Anniversary of the National Revolutionary Army's Vow to Launch the Northern Expedition 255

City Party Headquarters Convened Commemorative Meeting

All Sectors Must Send Representatives to Attend

Zhang Zhijiang Discussed the Closure of the Pacification Commissioner's Office Yesterday 257

Central Guoshu (National Martial Arts) Institute Establishes Guoshu Specialized School

Zhang Zhijiang, the Pacification Commissioner of Jiangsu, and Zhang Shusheng, the Chief of Staff of the Commissioner's Office, hosted a gathering at Gongdelin yesterday at noon, attended by over a hundred people. During the gathering, Commissioner Zhang reported that it has been eight months since he was appointed as Commissioner by the central government. The establishment of the Commissioner's Office was initially limited to four months before being disbanded, which was later extended for another four months. It will expire at the end of July. Although the central government has not expressed whether to retain or abolish it, the Commissioner's Office has already submitted a request to close it down. As for the suppression of bandits, the provincial government can handle it themselves. Therefore, after the Commissioner's Office is abolished, all matters will be transferred to the provincial government. The troops under his command, including the four divisions led by Liang Guanying, will not be transferred elsewhere for the time being and can still work hard to suppress bandits in Jiangsu Province. He expressed deep gratitude to everyone present for their efforts in assisting and hoped for continued support in quickly pacifying the bandits. He added that whether you are from Jiangsu or other provinces residing here, you should all be able to seek happiness for Jiangsu Province. He then reported the intention of establishing the Central Guoshu Institute to strengthen the nation and save the country, and to raise funds. The initiative was launched by Niu Tiesheng, Huang Jinrong, Du Yuesheng, Zhang Xiaolin, and others.

Agreement Reached on Weighs and Measures Inspection in Concessions 264

Previously Set Date Not To Be Extended

Shanghai's new weights and measures system was announced as uniform on July 1st, and it was scheduled to be inspected in stages by the Social Affairs and Public Security Bureaus starting on the 11th. An agreement has been reached on the inspection of the concessions. The details are as follows:

Concession Inspection 265

The weights and measures inspection is divided into four phases: Phase 1, the South Shanghai District; Phase 2, the Zhabei District; Phase 3, the Concession District; Phase 4, the Rural District. Regarding the inspection of the Public Concession, an agreement has been reached in general between Municipal Government Secretary-General Yu Hongjun and Shanghai Municipal Council Secretary General Fessenden. The Municipal Social Affairs Bureau will reconvene a meeting with the authorities of the Public Concession to discuss the date and procedures. Regarding the French Concession, an agreement has been reached between the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau and the French Concession Superintendent Weizhiren. Currently, the French Consul is seeking instructions from the French Minister to Beijing, Mr. de Martel. The date will be determined after a reply is received.

Holding as Scheduled 266

After the new weights and measures system was announced as uniform, trade associations such as the fresh meat industry, chicken and duck industry, cattle and sheep industry, soap industry, dried goods industry, sauce garden industry, and cotton cloth industry have all received new instruments from weights and measures equipment manufacturers. As for the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce's request to postpone the inspection and destroy the old instruments, it is heard that the office does not punish during inspections. After detecting violations, it only advises the use of new instruments. In fact, it only seeks to promote the destruction of old instruments and only applies this to those that are beyond repair. If a vegetable vendor's scale is found to be non-compliant during the inspection, it will be stamped with a non-compliant mark and ordered to be repaired. Therefore, it has been decided to hold the inspection as scheduled.

Public Groups Continue to Protest

Local Public Groups Jointly Petition

The Chinese National Anti-Narcotics Association believes that the establishment of the Opium Prohibition and Investigation Office by the Central Opium Prohibition Committee, which collects opium taxes and openly sells opium, is a clear violation of the Premier's legacy of rejecting drugs and the international opium prohibition treaty. Over the past week, various places have continued to express their opposition. Those belonging to party headquarters include the Tianjin City Party Headquarters, Siming County Party Headquarters, Minhou County Party Headquarters, Changshu County Party Headquarters, Wu County Party Headquarters, Shaoxing County Party Headquarters, Longyuan County Party Headquarters, Shangyu County Party Headquarters, Fengxian County Party Headquarters, Haiyan County Party Headquarters, Fuyang County Party Headquarters, Fenshui County Party Headquarters, Lanxi County Party Headquarters, etc. Those belonging to public groups include the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce, Shanghai Special City Federation of People's Associations, National Association of Chinese Christian Young Men's Association, National Association of Chinese Christian Young Women's Association, Shanghai Lawyers Association, World's Chinese Students' Federation, Shanghai Children's Lecture Troupe, Shaoxing Seven County Shanghai Association of Fellow Provincials, Anhui Shanghai Association of Fellow Provincials, Hua Yang Yi Zhen Association, Shanghai Women's Relief Association, Chinese Vocational Education Society, Chinese Christian Education Association, Chinese Leprosy Relief Association, Chinese Christian Encouragement Association, Shanghai Preaching Federation, Wenzhou Shanghai Association of Fellow Provincials, Henan Shanghai Association of Fellow Provincials, Changshu Shanghai Association of Fellow Provincials, Shanghai Jingwu Athletic Association, Shanghai Wuxue Association, Customs Chinese Staff Club, Xiamen Journalists Association, Xiaoshan County Farmers Association, Yin County Third District Office. In addition, anti-narcotics groups from remote areas are also preparing. There are many reports received by telegram every day. The above expressions are very intense. The response has been very good, and major groups have joined in one after another. It is scheduled to close at 4:00 PM today. Kidnappers in Wang Zhendshi Case Sentenced to Death 268

Physician Wang Zhendshi, the young master of Wang Yutai Tea House, practiced medicine at No. 411-2 Jingan Temple Road. At 11:15 AM on March 27th of this year, several kidnappers suddenly entered Wang's home under the pretense of seeking medical treatment, threatened him with guns, and abducted Wang Zhendshi. Later, Wang's family prepared a ransom of 20,000 yuan to redeem him. Hua Detectives Lu Liankui and Liu Shaokui of the General Inspectorate arrested three kidnappers, Zhu Xiangsheng, Xu Hongyi, and Gu Zhongfang, and sent them to the Special District Local Court. After several trials, the debate has concluded. The details have been repeatedly reported in this newspaper. Yesterday at noon, Judge Ge Zhitan arrived at Criminal Court No. 2 to announce the verdict. The main text reads: Zhu Xiangsheng is sentenced to death for the crime of jointly kidnapping and extorting a ransom, and deprived of his civil rights indefinitely. Xu Hongyi is sentenced to fifteen years of imprisonment for the crime of assisting others in extorting a ransom and deprived of his civil rights indefinitely. The number of days of detention before the trial is determined shall be deducted from the sentence at a rate of two days for one day of imprisonment. Gu Zhongfang is sentenced to life imprisonment for the crime of jointly kidnapping and extorting a ransom and deprived of his civil rights indefinitely. The recovered贓洋 of 110 yuan, plus 100 yuan, is confiscated.

Chen Genjiang's Unrequited Love Leads to Planned Poisoning 269

Obtains a Packet of Unslaked Lime

Plots to Blind Xia Amao

Chen Genjiang, from Chongming, lives at No. 1512 Jiaxing Road. His daughter, Chen Amao, is eighteen years old and has a decent appearance. A man from Haimen, Lu Jinwen, twenty-one years old, who is still single, has been coveting Amao for a long time and wants to marry her. However, Amao has already been betrothed to someone else, and Lu Jinwen has been tempting her in every way, but has not been able to fulfill his wish. On the 4th of this month, he said to the girl, "If you don't agree to come with me and be my wife, I will use lime to blind your eyes." Amao resolutely refused, and Lu left in hatred. Fearing that he would actually carry out this vicious act, Amao reported it to the Harbin Police Station. The next morning, Lu met Amao's father, Chen Genjiang, on the road and said, "Your daughter Amao has slept with me twice. Please don't be 元龍高臥 [indifferent], and quickly marry Amao to me, otherwise there will be unfavorable consequences." After speaking, he fled. Chen returned home and questioned his daughter. Amao firmly stated that nothing of the sort had happened, and that Lu's words were completely fabricated. Later, her older sister, Fengmei, also asked Amao whether she had any ambiguous relationship with Lu twice. Amao said that if she had lost her virginity to Lu, she would buy incense and candles and swear to Heaven. The next day, while Chen Genjiang and Amao were out, Lu sneaked into their home and tried his best to persuade Chen Fengmei to marry Amao to him, or to run away from her father, but was scolded by Fengmei and left. Lu then decided to use a poisonous hand and bought a packet of unslaked lime from a certain place. At around 10:00 AM the day before yesterday, he rushed to Amao's home, intending to blind her eyes. Unexpectedly, the girl's father, Chen Genjiang, saw Lu Jinwen arriving with a paper bag and knew his intentions. He tried to capture him, but Lu could not resist and dropped the bag and fled. Chen chased after him for about dozens of yards and was intercepted by Hua Police No. 3133, who arrested him along with the lime bag and took him to the police station for detention. Yesterday morning, he was sent to the Third Criminal Court of the Special District Court. Police Lawyer Li Zhishan presented the case and stated that investigations revealed that the defendant had previously committed theft and robbery and was sentenced to two years and seven months of imprisonment. He was also sentenced to fifteen days of detention for soliciting prostitutes. He asked the court to take this into consideration and presented the lime bag as evidence. Amao then stated that the defendant used to be her neighbor, so they knew each other. He often came to her house to look around and tease her, and briefly described the situation. Her father, Chen Genjiang, and her sister, Fengmei, also testified to the previous situation. When questioned by the defendant, his confession was vague and he denied the allegations. Judge Feng Shide reviewed the confession and ordered him to be remanded in custody for further investigation and questioning.

United States Purchases Eight Thousand Head of Cattle in China 270

For Use as Food

Japanese Suffer Blow

Qingdao Port has the largest export of beef every year. The beef in Shandong Province is praised and bought by foreigners. Japanese companies have established special transportation companies in Qingdao to purchase Chinese beef for export, with annual shipments amounting to several million yuan. Recently, the United States has been buying food beef in Shandong, which has aroused jealousy among the Japanese. The first shipment of cattle to the United States is scheduled to depart from Shanghai. The details are as follows:

Japanese Dominance 271

The largest export from Qingdao to the East is Shandong beef, which is transported by ships from Japanese mail companies such as Osaka and Harada. It is not certain whether live cattle or slaughtered meat is transported. The Japanese have historically held a dominant position in the export of Shandong beef in Jiaozhou.

American Merchants Run Chinese Cattle 272

This year, American merchants have specially come to Qingdao to purchase a large number of food cattle. Mr. Luo Meng, an American in Qingdao, has placed an order with Shandong cattle merchant Hui Xing. It is heard that a total of 8,000 head of Shandong cattle have been purchased for consumption by Americans. It is planned to ship them to the United States in ten batches.

Allocate Naval Vessels 273

Of the 8,000 cattle purchased, 1,000 will be slaughtered in batches in Qingdao and supplied to naval vessels in China and Luzon. All deliveries will be made in Qingdao. The remaining 7,000 will be shipped directly to New York in North America.

First Shipment 274

The first batch of cattle to be shipped to the United States has been agreed upon by the American merchants and Hui Xing to ship 700 head first. However, due to the long distance across the ocean, it has been decided to slaughter them in Qingdao and transport the beef in the refrigerated compartments of the ship, which can still maintain its freshness. The first shipment is scheduled for the 15th of this month, and a ship will be dispatched from Shanghai to Qingdao to act as an agent. After this incident, Japanese cattle exporters are strongly opposed because it has broken their monopoly and raised beef prices.

Jianghai Customs Burns Opium 280

Yesterday, the Jianghai Customs held a burning of prohibited opium and drugs at the customs warehouse pier in Lujiazui, Pudong. Apart from the Garrison Headquarters, the National Anti-Drug Association, and the Shanghai County Government, whose representatives did not attend, the following officials were present: Ni Guangzu of the Shanghai Special District Court, Wang Zhizhong of the District Court, Wang Zongjian of the Customs Superintendent's Office, Huang Chen of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, etc. Cai Zanzhou, a section member of the Third District of the Public Security Bureau, temporarily led a platoon of armed police officers to maintain order. At 9:00 AM, Ge Yixin, a translator from the Customs, together with Mr. Roberts, a Westerner from the Transportation Department, supervised laborers to load the various drugs onto a small ferry to cross the river. After weighing and verifying that there were no errors, they were successively thrown into the kiln for burning. This was completed at noon. A total of two large wooden boxes of heroin were destroyed, weighing 6,612 taels, valued at 331,420 yuan; 7 dan, 9 jin, and 12 taels of opium, valued at 29,716 yuan and 3 jiao; 32 dan and 90 jin of poppy shells, valued at 493 yuan and 5 jiao; morphine pills totaling 6,612 taels, valued at 2,418 yuan and 1 jiao; and drug paraphernalia valued at 43 yuan and 2 jiao. In addition, there were also two boxes of roulette gambling equipment and two packages of Chinese and Western communist books, which were also thrown into the kiln for burning. The above-mentioned prohibited drugs were seized by search teams on various ships within a three-month period from March 21st to June 20th of this year.

Wusong Water Patrol Team Recovers Stolen Valuable Cotton Yarn 281

Yonghe Trading Company at 268 North Suzhou Road in this city consigned 32 pieces of cotton yarn, valued at over 10,000 yuan, to a barge owned by Cao Guan'gen. The barge was moored at the Bund of Beijing Road, intending to transfer the goods to the Dadong Steamer of the Dada Company in the South City for unloading. However, the barge suddenly went missing on the evening of the 5th, and despite searching everywhere, its whereabouts were unknown. Subsequently, the barge captain, Cao Guan'gen, claimed that he feared that the first mate, Jin Hai, had absconded with it. He immediately reported to the Water Patrol Police Station and the Municipal Public Security Bureau's Water Patrol Team to conduct a strict search, and also placed a reward notice in the newspaper for his capture. At around 5:00 AM the day before yesterday, Ding Xiaoping, the leader of the Fourth Detachment of the Municipal Public Security Bureau's Water Patrol Team in Wusong, led his team on patrol in the Huangpu River area. While patrolling in a small harbor opposite the Guanghua Oil Depot in Gaoqiao, they caught sight of a barge moored there, unguarded. Upon inspection of the cargo, they found that it was all cotton yarn. Knowing that it was the lost cargo of Yonghe Trading Company, they carefully took inventory, counting 27 pieces. However, as it was low tide at the time, the ship was stranded on the shoal and could not be moved. Later, the tide rose that evening, and the ship was towed to Wusong and impounded. Yesterday, Leader Ding had already reported to the Shanghai General Team to request instructions on how to proceed.

Woman Sues for Property of Two Inns 282

Yesterday, a woman named Zhang Jinbao, represented by a lawyer, filed a criminal lawsuit with the French Court, claiming that the plaintiff's birth mother, Zhang Laoer, nicknamed "Antique Laoer," had been running the Huaxing and Xindengfeng inns on Avenue Edward VII for many years. Unexpectedly, after Laoer passed away due to illness in 1928, all the land and buildings of the two inns and all movable property were seized by the bookkeeper Zhou Heshang alone, ignoring her claims. This constitutes the crime of encroachment, and she requests an investigation and the return of all property. The defendant also retained a lawyer to argue that the Huaxing and Xindengfeng inns were indeed opened by Zhang Laoer. The Huaxing Inn was merged into the Xindengfeng Inn due to demolition and reconstruction. When Zhang Laoer was critically ill in April 1928, fearing that there would be no one to take care of her two sons and all her property after her death, she entrusted Lawyer Jiao Kun to make a will, placing her two sons and the business of the inns under the management of the defendant Zhou Heshang, who would raise the two sons and then return the property. There is a will to prove this. He questions whether the plaintiff is Zhang Laoer's daughter, as Zhang Laoer never mentioned it during her lifetime, and the defendant has never even seen the plaintiff's face. The plaintiff's claim is without evidence, and he requests that the case be dismissed. Judge Zhu instructed that witnesses be summoned to court for further questioning and verification.

Accomplice in Robbery of Wages Apprehended 283

Liu Huicheng, a native of Nanjing and the accountant of the Tianzhang Paper Mill at the Yangshupu Wharf, withdrew over 1,000 yuan in banknotes at the factory's office at 38 Avenue Edward VII on the afternoon of the day before yesterday to pay wages. He took a public bus back to the factory. After getting off the bus at Dalian Bay Road in Yangshupu, he had only walked a few steps when four bandits stabbed him in the head with knives, causing him to fall to the ground, and robbed him of 1,258 yuan in banknotes, fleeing in different directions. As a result, one bandit, named Liu Ji, a native of Qingkou, was captured, and 350 yuan in stolen banknotes were found on him. He was taken to the Hongkou Police Station. The injured victim was sent to the Tongren Hospital for treatment. This incident has already been reported in the newspaper. Subsequently, Chinese Detective Liu Baoshan apprehended another accomplice, Xu Abao, a native of Ningbo, at a certain address in Renshou Lane on Avenue Petain. A search revealed no stolen money, only two small knives. He was taken to the police station. Yesterday morning, they were jointly escorted to the Third Criminal Court of the Special District Court. Police lawyer Li Zhishan presented the case and requested a postponement. The stolen banknotes were presented for inspection. Liu Kunjin, a native of Zhili, testified that he happened to be passing by the cinema and saw many people and heard cries of "Catch the thief!" The defendant was running wildly, and he was stopped by him. The stolen banknotes presented were found in his hand and on the ground. However, the victim, Liu Huicheng, was discharged from the hospital after the doctor bandaged his wounds and is currently recuperating at home, so he did not appear in court to testify. When questioned, Liu Ji confessed that he was selling peaches near the cinema and found the banknotes on the ground. He did not steal them. Xu Abao confessed that he sells Jiaolun cakes and knew nothing about the robbery. The two knives presented were used for cutting cakes. He begged for leniency. Judge Feng Shide reviewed the confessions and ordered the two defendants to be remanded in custody and the case to be investigated and questioned at a later date.

Police Officer Electrocuted in Heavy Rain 284

Electrocution from Bedside Lamp

His Wife Narrowly Escapes

Wu Jincheng, a native of Qingjiang and a Chinese police officer with badge number 1580 in the Hongkou Police Station, lived at 276 Dayou Lane, Ruijin Road. At around 7:00 AM the day before yesterday, during a heavy rain with thunder and lightning, Officer Wu was sleeping in bed. Because he lived downstairs, there was five or six inches of accumulated water, and there was an electrical leakage from the bedside lamp. Wu was electrocuted. His wife witnessed this and rushed to pull her husband down, but she was also electrocuted. When family members heard the commotion, they immediately turned off the power. His brother, Wu Jinshan, also a Chinese police officer with badge number 1187, arrived and took the couple to the Public Works Department Hospital for treatment. Wu's wife suffered a lighter shock and was not seriously injured, but Wu Jincheng died before he could be treated. The hospital notified the police station, which sent detectives to investigate. The body was taken to the Pylon Road mortuary. Yesterday morning, Prosecutor Guo Wei of the Special District Court was commissioned to examine the body. He opened the case and, after questioning Wu Jinshan and others, concluded that the deceased Wu Jincheng died from electrocution before his death. The body was released to his brother for burial.

Foreign Shipping Companies on the Sichuan River Maintain Equilibrium 285

Freight Rates Not Falling

Proceeding According to Plan

Various foreign merchants in this city believe that the competition among shipping companies on the Sichuan River is too fierce, leading to a sharp drop in freight rates. Furthermore, Chinese merchants' ships are also operating direct routes to Shen and Yu, causing significant damage to the shipping between Shanghai, Hankou, Yichang, and between Yichang and Chongqing. The foreign merchants have been meeting for several days. They have recognized that the freight rates for cotton yarn on the Sichuan River have fallen to the point where they cannot be reduced any further. If they fall any lower, the losses will be even greater. Yesterday, a reporter learned that the foreign merchants have reached a final decision: they will change their strategy of lowering prices to maintaining equilibrium. They have agreed that the freight rates for direct shipments of yarn from Shanghai to Chongqing will not be lower than those of Chinese ships, in order to eliminate the price war in the Yangtze River shipping industry and to achieve mutually beneficial cooperation with Chinese ships upstream. They have completely abandoned the previous strategy of price competition and have switched to a more positive approach of operating according to plan.

Recent News from the Sichuan Railway Shareholders' Association 286

A National Telegram Was Sent Yesterday

Since the first preparatory meeting of the Sichuan Railway Shareholders' Association in Shanghai on July 2nd at Bansong Garden, where Wu Hua, Duan Zhishu, Tan Fu, Tan Jiqing, Yao Banghua, Zhang Menglin, and Ge Manyin were elected as preparatory committee members, they have been very busy these days with clarifying the whereabouts of the share funds and monitoring the actions of the corrupt railway officials. Yesterday, they sent an express telegram, describing in great detail the inside story of the Sichuan-Hankou Railway Company. Here is an excerpt: (Omitted above) "We, in order to protect shareholders' rights and eliminate the chaos in Sichuan, have voluntarily initiated the Sichuan Railway Shareholders' Association in Shanghai as the first step for shareholders to exercise their rights. On June 2nd, the first general meeting was held in Shanghai, and the following important resolutions were passed: (1) Fundamentally deny the dissolved board of directors, which has lost its effectiveness, and all illegally appointed false three managers, and send those who openly disregard shareholders and use their names for evil deeds to the authorities for strict investigation according to law. (2) Shareholders in various counties in Sichuan and other places should voluntarily initiate shareholders' associations to further promote a general meeting of all Sichuan shareholders to fundamentally resolve all issues of the company. (3) All existing property and evidence of the company should be cleared and properly handed over to a reliable bank for safekeeping. No one shall dispose of them until after the formal shareholders' meeting is convened. (4) The loan bonds issued by the Bank of Communications should be ordered by the authorities to be handed over by Xie Chi and handled in accordance with the third proposal. A letter should also be sent to the Bank of Communications stating that no funds should be handed over unless a legally responsible person is produced by the company. (5) Urge the past responsible persons of the company to announce the accounts and hand over the accounting records. At the same time, shareholders should investigate the evidence of the corrupt railway officials embezzling share funds and submit it to the shareholders' meeting for thorough investigation. (6) If the frustrated warlords and politicians who intend to erode the share funds still do not repent, their various conspiracies and crimes will be exposed and the National Government will be asked to arrest them. (7) The 2.7 million yuan owed to the company by the Ministry of Railways should not be requested to be transferred to other uses before the shareholders' meeting is convened, and especially should not be interfered with by the Sichuan military and political authorities. (8) This company is of a commercial nature and has full autonomy. No illegal interference from any individual or organization outside the shareholders is permitted. We will spare no effort to achieve these eight points. However, we fear that our strength is weak and that we will not be able to achieve much. We hope that all virtuous people will uphold justice and give us candid advice, and that shareholders in various places will work together to advance our cause and support us so that the future of the Sichuan Railway will have a glimmer of hope and will not be robbed by villains. This telegram is respectfully submitted for your clear instructions. The Sichuan Railway Shareholders' Association in Shanghai, sealed with a yang seal."

Automobile News

Essay

Ford Study Notes 317

— De Xin

My experience with automobile studies is quite shallow, but I have a strong passion for it. Therefore, I have been engaged in automobile research and learning. Aside from attending a specialized automobile school in Shanghai for less than a year, I have not had many opportunities to study and learn from automobile experts.

Fortunately, the Ford Motor Company of Pudong, Shanghai, has a service school established this year on May 18th. Through the introduction of Manager Lu, I was able to enter the school for more practical training. Although the time was short, I benefited a lot. I must thank teacher Mr. Yu Tengmao and the Ford Company's rich equipment, as well as Manager Lu's enthusiastic introduction. Now, I will briefly describe my six weeks in school, as well as the various excellent and enthusiastic training, to tell the gentlemen who enjoy reading automobile news.

China's automobile industry is still in its infancy. All vehicles needed are purchased from Europe and the United States, and there is no other way to obtain this transportation tool that travels like electricity and surges like clouds. As a result, foreign automobile manufacturers can easily obtain this large Eastern market without any effort. Therefore, all patriotic Chinese people who see this transportation marvel but cannot salvage the situation must rise up and strive to realize the dream of a Chinese automobile factory and reverse this recession. This is why I abandoned my teaching career and ventured into this darkness, hoping to find something. Since there are no good facilities in the country, I have to rely on foreign commercialized technical schools. This is similar to when Western missionary schools had a greater influence when our country's school education began. In Shanghai, there are many European and American automobile manufacturers seeking to sell their products here. In particular, the American Ford factory has come to our country and established a large-scale operation. Its management and sales will probably be in the first position. Recently, there have even been proposals to establish a factory in China for manufacturing. Therefore, in terms of publicity, vehicle owner services, repair parts, and technical training, there are complete plans to meet the various needs of society. This is why there is a service school, specifically to train technicians from various agencies who already have rich experience, and teach them the proper Ford repair methods, the proper use of special tools, and a correct understanding of the planning and principles of Ford engineers' designs. It also tells them the methods of managing Ford, and the rules of managing the factory. Therefore, no tuition or miscellaneous fees are charged. Except for not providing wages, the workers are managed in the same way as the factory's workers. However, they must be introduced by related factories, and they must be able to strictly abide by the factory's rules and have considerable car knowledge before they are allowed to enter the school.

Mr. Yu Tengfang is from Guangdong. He specialized in automobile studies in the United States for nearly ten years and worked at the Ford factory. Later, he served as an engineer at the factory for many years. Recently, he was sent back to China as a traveling representative of the Ford factory in China, and also as a teacher at the service school. Mr. Yu is humorous, lively, and extremely enthusiastic. He instructs for eight hours a day without ever tiring. Although he is extremely busy, he never stops lecturing and demonstrating. He is very skilled in both theory and technology. He is not someone who can only talk eloquently or only knows one aspect of the job. Therefore, all the students' questions can be answered very satisfactorily. The following is a description of my studies at the school:

(1) Entering and Leaving the Factory: Every morning at 7:30, I took the free ferry provided by the Da Lai Company from the Customs Wharf on the Bund in Huangpu to the Da Lai Wharf in Pudong. The Ford Company is located on the left side of the Da Lai Company. When entering the factory, I had to wear a badge to show the gatekeeper, and record the time of entry and exit on the time clock machine using my personal card. Then, I entered the changing room to change into work clothes, and at 8:15, the work horn sounded. Each time, Mr. Yu would call the roll. There were about thirty students in my class, all from different places. Some had worked in the automobile industry for seven or eight years, and some for two or three years, while others were not very knowledgeable. Therefore, the results were also not good. At 12:00, I left the factory for lunch. The time was limited to only thirty minutes, so it was very rushed. After lunch, I worked until 4:30 in the afternoon. I washed my hands and changed clothes, and at 4:45, I followed the routine of recording the time of leaving the factory on my card. I then took the Da Lai small ferry back to Puxi. I did this five days a week, except for Saturday, which was a holiday. I worked eight hours a day without any rest or slackness. There were no chairs or benches to sit on, except for standing and squatting. Even when I had to take notes, I could only bend my knees and lean over to do so. Needless to say, my clothes, shoes, hands, and face were always stained with oil. However, the factory grounds, machinery, and tools had to be carefully cleaned and arranged. Therefore, before leaving the factory every day, I had to sweep thoroughly and clean with a broom. As a result, what I saw every morning when I entered the factory was extremely clean and refreshing, as if it had just been set up and no one had ever worked there before. Mr. Yu repeatedly reminded us of this cleaning item.

(2) Factory and Equipment: The school's area is less than one-sixteenth of the entire factory. I estimate its area to be within 15 square zhang. It contains a Ford generator, which is the source of all electricity for the headquarters. All the machinery in the room is equipped with a dynamo for charging and starting. The following items are equipped as follows: air compressor, cylinder lathe, valve repair machine, nailing machine, grinding machine, whetstone machine, old-style transformer testing machine, motor testing machine, lifting machine, engine repair frame, rear axle frame, hydraulic press, charger, steel workbench, and five large cabinets filled with special tools for repairing new and old-style passenger cars and trucks. It is said that all the tools and machinery are worth more than 20,000 yuan. These are stored specifically for the use of the school and are the same as any Ford repair shop in the world. In China, only this set is the most complete. If a new method is invented, a tool will be sent here for backup.

(3) Practice and Repair: First, each person is given a copy of the Ford parts catalog (printed by Central Wenhe) to familiarize students with the names of the parts, and a book on the essentials of managing the new Ford. On the first and second days, the prepared engines are disassembled in groups to familiarize themselves with the arrangement of each part. Since the students who came here already had considerable preparation, they had a concrete concept after one or two disassemblies. On the third day, a new-style passenger car, which had traveled more than 16,000 miles, was delivered from outside the factory. This was an excellent object for practice and repair. After being placed on the lifting machine, the engine was started, and they were taught the various procedures for testing the engine. Then, it was disassembled part by part. First, the engine part was tested. This engine alone took ten days for detailed inspection and repair. Every part was inspected to within one-thousandth of an inch. If any part was specified to be within three-thousandths of an inch, it had to be repaired, or cast with alloy, or have shims added, or replaced with a new one. All modifications and additions were made in accordance with the prescribed procedures. Even the slightest use of a wrench had to be done with the prescribed type of wrench. No borrowing or swapping was allowed. It was definitely not comparable to using an adjustable wrench as if it were omnipotent. When assembling, in addition to the commonly known wrench screw force, there were many other tools used. In short, the reason for using so many tools was to facilitate assembly, save time and effort, and especially to avoid damaging the parts. It was determined that this car's cylinder car was more than five-thousandths of an inch. The pistons, piston rings, and valves were partially replaced with new ones. Other parts, such as the electrical system's charging, wiring, and generator repair, the ignition system's adjustment, the fuel system's and oil system's inspection, cleaning, and adjustment, and the frame and brakes were all carefully inspected and repaired. All rust was repainted. After three weeks, except for the appearance being inferior to a new car, the internal parts were said by Mr. Yu to be no different from a new car. He also said that sometimes external repairs do not need to be so troublesome or so thorough. However, in a true Ford repair shop, it is not permissible to treat car owners carelessly. After this car left the factory, another car was disassembled and repaired step by step, with all the necessary parts being done in a week, and detailed instructions on the principles, designs, and dimensions were given to ensure proficiency. Any questions were asked during these two weeks. Sometimes, they were listed on a small blackboard. Students would write down important points with a pencil whenever they were mentioned. Therefore, there was no need for a general blackboard lecture style. If you didn't pay attention, you would miss the opportunity to take notes. Mr. Yu did not lecture at a fixed time or place, and he did not want to repeat what he had already said. Therefore, it was necessary to pay attention at all times. Occasionally, a gentle request would be made, and Mr. Yu might repeat himself in a rambling manner.

(4) Testing and Visiting: After the various courses were completed, the students were tasked with inspecting and repairing a truck that was not starting properly, until it started successfully. This was a stage where Mr. Yu deliberately introduced many problems to test the students. When doing so, Mr. Yu would laugh and say that the designated person was responsible for correcting it. This was one of the most interesting parts of the course. The second was a verbal question and answer session. All the repair procedures and verbal regulations that had been taught in the past were asked in turn to each person, one question at a time.

On another day, he spoke about the history of automobiles and the various situations in the Ford factory. I began to understand the greatness of its plans and the beauty of its setup. I couldn't help but be amazed. He also showed Ford's specially made film to teach us how to manage its business and various sales methods. Unfortunately, Ford's factory work was already being shipped to Hankou and I was unable to see the whole picture. In the film I saw, there was also a section where engines flowed out of the launch pad like water, ready for grinding. Tools circled in the air like dancing in the air, ready to be taken. There was no suffering from running around. It is appropriate that in April of this year, its car production reached more than 121,000 units. When I entered the school, Mr. Yu led us to visit the factory's parts storage, which was divided into new and old passenger and freight parts, a carpentry department, a paint thinning department, and a battery manufacturing department. Although the factory staff was not large, it was orderly and clean. On the last day, he also led us to visit the various departments of the Meitong Company, which manages Ford in Shanghai, to verify what we had learned. After the visit, the course ended, and it was time for teachers and friends to say goodbye. Before leaving the factory, each person was given a Ford Service School commemorative badge and a certificate issued by the Ford Company. Although the time was short, there was a reluctance to say goodbye among the teachers and friends. Mr. Yu was very knowledgeable, and although he sometimes used humor and sarcasm, he was always willing to take care of us and explain things in detail, which made it difficult for us to forget his enthusiasm and sincerity. Therefore, one evening, I invited some classmates to have dinner and take pictures at the Great East to commemorate the occasion.

Recorded in Shanghai on July 5, 1938.

— Xiao Guoxiang

Yesterday, I received a statistical report on the American automobile industry of the past year from the New York Automobile Chamber of Commerce. It details the relationship of the industry with other sectors. I was very pleased to read it. The year 1930 was a year of unfavorable economic conditions worldwide, and especially in the United States.
